<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Animal husbandry</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Management, <a href="/wiki/Selective_breeding" title="Selective breeding">selective breeding</a> and care of farm animals by humans</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cattle_Feedlot_near_Rocky_Ford,_CO_IMG_5651-2.jpg"><img alt="Cattle feedlot" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2814" data-file-width="3858" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cattle_Feedlot_near_Rocky_Ford%2C_CO_IMG_5651-2.jpg/300px-Cattle_Feedlot_near_Rocky_Ford%2C_CO_IMG_5651-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cattle_Feedlot_near_Rocky_Ford%2C_CO_IMG_5651-2.jpg/450px-Cattle_Feedlot_near_Rocky_Ford%2C_CO_IMG_5651-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cattle_Feedlot_near_Rocky_Ford%2C_CO_IMG_5651-2.jpg/600px-Cattle_Feedlot_near_Rocky_Ford%2C_CO_IMG_5651-2.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cattle_Feedlot_near_Rocky_Ford,_CO_IMG_5651-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cattle feedlot in <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, USA</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Broiler_house.jpg"><img alt="Chickens" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="427" data-file-width="640" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Broiler_house.jpg/300px-Broiler_house.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Broiler_house.jpg/450px-Broiler_house.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Broiler_house.jpg/600px-Broiler_house.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Broiler_house.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Raising chickens intensively for meat in a broiler house, USA</div></div></div>
<p><b>Animal husbandry</b> is the branch of <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> concerned with animals that are raised for <a href="/wiki/Meat" title="Meat">meat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Animal_fiber" title="Animal fiber">fibre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">milk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egg" title="Egg">eggs</a>, or other products. It includes day-to-day care, <a href="/wiki/Selective_breeding" title="Selective breeding">selective breeding</a> and the raising of <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a>.
</p><p>Husbandry has a long history, starting with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neolithic_revolution" title="Neolithic revolution">Neolithic revolution</a> when animals were first <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">domesticated</a>, from around 13,000 BC onwards, antedating farming of the first crops. By the time of early civilisations such as <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">ancient Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">cattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheep" title="Sheep">sheep</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goat" title="Goat">goats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pig" title="Pig">pigs</a> were being raised on farms.
</p><p>Major changes took place in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbian_Exchange" title="Columbian Exchange">Columbian Exchange</a> when Old World livestock were brought to the New World, and then in the <a href="/wiki/British_Agricultural_Revolution" title="British Agricultural Revolution">British Agricultural Revolution</a> of the 18th century, when livestock breeds like the <a href="/wiki/English_Longhorn" title="English Longhorn">Dishley Longhorn</a> cattle and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lincoln_(sheep)" title="Lincoln (sheep)">Lincoln Longwool</a> sheep were rapidly improved by agriculturalists such as <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bakewell_(agriculturalist)" title="Robert Bakewell (agriculturalist)">Robert Bakewell</a> to yield more meat, milk, and <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">wool</a>.
</p><p>A wide range of other species such as <a href="/wiki/Horse" title="Horse">horse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_buffalo" title="Water buffalo">water buffalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Llama" title="Llama">llama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabbit" title="Rabbit">rabbit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guinea_pig" title="Guinea pig">guinea pig</a> are used as livestock in some parts of the world. <a href="/wiki/Insect_farming" title="Insect farming">Insect farming</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Aquaculture" title="Aquaculture">aquaculture</a> of <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mollusc" title="Mollusc">molluscs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Crustacean" title="Crustacean">crustaceans</a>, is widespread.
</p><p>Modern animal husbandry relies on <a href="/wiki/Agriculture#Livestock_production_systems" title="Agriculture">production systems</a> adapted to the type of land available. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subsistence_farming" title="Subsistence farming">Subsistence farming</a> is being superseded by <a href="/wiki/Intensive_animal_farming" title="Intensive animal farming">intensive animal farming</a> in the more developed parts of the world, where for example beef cattle are kept in high density <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feedlots" title="Feedlots">feedlots</a>, and thousands of <a href="/wiki/Chicken" title="Chicken">chickens</a> may be raised in broiler houses or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battery_farm" title="Battery farm">batteries</a>. On poorer soil such as in uplands, animals are often kept more extensively, and may be allowed to roam widely, foraging for themselves.
</p><p>Most livestock are <a href="/wiki/Herbivore" title="Herbivore">herbivores</a>, except for pigs and chickens which are <a href="/wiki/Omnivore" title="Omnivore">omnivores</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ruminantia" title="Ruminantia">Ruminants</a> like cattle and sheep are adapted to feed on grass; they can forage outdoors, or may be fed entirely or in part on rations richer in energy and protein, such as pelleted cereals. Pigs and poultry cannot digest the <a href="/wiki/Cellulose" title="Cellulose">cellulose</a> in forage, and require cereals and other high-energy foods.
</p>
